<p>The <b>Technische Universität Darmstadt</b> (unofficially <b>Technical University of Darmstadt</b> or <b>Darmstadt University of Technology</b>), commonly referred to as <b>TU Darmstadt</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> in the city of <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt" title="Darmstadt">Darmstadt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>. It was founded in 1877 and received the right to award doctorates in 1899.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> In 1882, it was the first university in the world to set up a chair in <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>. In 1883, the university founded the first faculty for electrical engineering and introduced the world's first course of study in electrical engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-:10_5-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:21_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:21-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> In 2004, it became the first German university to be declared as an autonomous university.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> Nobel laureate <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a> recommended this university.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>TU Darmstadt is a partner of the National Research Center for Applied Cybersecurity (CRISP), a collaboration between TU Darmstadt, <a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Institute for Secure Information Technology</a>, Fraunhofer Institute for Computer Graphics Research and the <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Darmstadt University of Applied Sciences">University of Applied Sciences Darmstadt</a>. With over 450 researchers working on topics related to security and privacy, this partnership represents the largest alliance of research institutes in the area of cybersecurity within Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> TU Darmstadt is also a member of the Competence Center for Applied Security Technology (CAST), the largest corporate network for cyber security in German-speaking countries.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TU Darmstadt is a member of <a href="/wiki/TU9" title="TU9">TU9</a>, a network of the most notable German <i><a href="/wiki/Technische_Hochschule" title="Technische Hochschule">Technische Universitäten</a></i> (universities of technology) and of the <a href="/wiki/Top_Industrial_Managers_for_Europe" title="Top Industrial Managers for Europe">Top Industrial Managers for Europe</a> network, which allows for student exchanges between leading engineering schools.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">Computer science</a>, <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence,</a> <a href="/wiki/Mechatronics" title="Mechatronics">mechatronics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Business_informatics" title="Business informatics">business informatics</a> and many more courses were introduced as scientific disciplines in Germany by Darmstadt faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-:10_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> Graduates of the TU Darmstadt include Nobel Prize winners, entrepreneurs, managers, billionaires and politicians. TU Darmstadt is one of the universities with the most <a href="/wiki/DAX" title="DAX">DAX</a> executive board members among its graduates.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Of the three German scientists who have been awarded a <a href="/wiki/Wolf_Prize_in_Physics" title="Wolf Prize in Physics">Wolf Prize in Physics</a>, two are graduates of the TU Darmstadt.  
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:180px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse,_KG_(26799455549).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse%2C_KG_%2826799455549%29.jpg/178px-HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse%2C_KG_%2826799455549%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="178" height="274" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse%2C_KG_%2826799455549%29.jpg/267px-HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse%2C_KG_%2826799455549%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse%2C_KG_%2826799455549%29.jpg/356px-HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse%2C_KG_%2826799455549%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="832" data-file-height="1280" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HRH_the_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse,_KG_(26799455549).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Louis IV, Grand Duke of Hesse-Darmstadt</div></div></div>
<p>On 10 October 1877, <a href="/wiki/Louis_IV,_Grand_Duke_of_Hesse" title="Louis IV, Grand Duke of Hesse">Louis IV, Grand Duke of Hesse</a>, elevated the <i>Polytechnische Schule</i> to <b><a href="/wiki/Technische_Hochschule" title="Technische Hochschule">Technische Hochschule</a> zu Darmstadt</b> and thereby raised the status of this educational institution to that of a university so that the <i><a href="/wiki/Abitur" title="Abitur">Abitur</a></i> (a school leaving certificate from German <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(Germany)" title="Gymnasium (Germany)">Gymnasium schools</a> qualifying for university admission or matriculation) became a requirement for admissions.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> In 1899, the <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i> was granted the right to award doctorates.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_beginnings">Early beginnings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early beginnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The University's history is varied: its early phases began with the <i>Höhere Gewerbschule</i> (Higher Trade School), which was founded in 1836 and received its own building near the 'Altes Pädagog' on Kapellplatz in 1844, followed by the <i>Technische Schule</i> (Technical School) in 1864 and the <i>Großherzoglich Hessische Polytechnische Schule</i> (Grand Ducal Hessian Polytechnic) in 1868. At that time, heated discussions were continually held in political circles on the issue as to whether such a poor state as the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Hesse" title="Grand Duchy of Hesse">Grand Duchy of Hessen</a> could afford a technically oriented higher educational institution, or even a polytechnic. After the foundation of <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i> in 1877, student numbers kept on being so low that in the years from 1881 to 1882 there were long debates in public about closing down the university. In this difficult situation, the local government and the university made the courageous decision to set up the first chair of <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a> worldwide. Thus the Faculty of Electrical Engineering came into being as the sixth faculty of the <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i>, which was a novelty in academia, because until then no other university had had such a faculty. This forward-looking higher education policy paved the way for Darmstadt to take up a leading position in the rapidly developing field of electrical engineering, which in turn led to a continuously rising number of students, so that the closure of the university never was demanded again.<sup id="cite_ref-:17_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:17-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:16_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:16-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="First_steps_as_a_university">First steps as a university</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: First steps as a university">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1895, new buildings were opened in Hochschulstrasse: the <i>Altes Hauptgebäude</i> (the 'Old Main Building' of the University) and an institute building directly opposite. During the two decades before the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, all disciplines of the university underwent diversification and expansion. New disciplines such as paper making and cellulose chemistry were introduced, and as early as 1913 a Chair of <a href="/wiki/Aeronautics" title="Aeronautics">Aeronautics</a> and Flight Mechanics was set up.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Meanwhile, the political climate had become stormier, and a growing political polarization exploded in Darmstadt over the question of foreign students. The <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i> had an extraordinarily large number of foreign students. In 1906, for instance, as many as three quarters of the electrical engineering students were from abroad, mainly from states of eastern Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>After the <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> there was an urgent need for reform of the education system at <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i>, which was seen as a prerequisite for meeting the requirements of a modern industrial society. Intense discussions were held on the aim of extending the <a href="/wiki/Curriculum" title="Curriculum">curriculum</a> beyond the purely technical education in order to prepare the engineer for his leading role in society. A concrete step in this direction was taken in 1924, when the 'General Faculty', which until then had combined all the non-technical subjects, was divided into a Department of Mathematics and Natural Science and a Department of Cultural Studies and Political Science. Moreover, the measures taken to provide students with knowledge outside their own field of study included the upgrading of Economics and the creation of professorships in political science, history of technology and sociology.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:17_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:17-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:16_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:16-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:18_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:18-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Restart_after_WW_II">Restart after WW II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Restart after WW II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:272px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Adler,_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude,_TU_Darmstadt.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Adler%2C_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude%2C_TU_Darmstadt.jpg/270px-Adler%2C_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude%2C_TU_Darmstadt.jpg" decoding="async" width="270" height="203" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Adler%2C_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude%2C_TU_Darmstadt.jpg/405px-Adler%2C_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude%2C_TU_Darmstadt.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ac/Adler%2C_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude%2C_TU_Darmstadt.jpg/540px-Adler%2C_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude%2C_TU_Darmstadt.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Adler,_Robert-Piloty-Geb%C3%A4ude,_TU_Darmstadt.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Eagle above the rear main entry to the Robert Piloty Building, nowadays home to the Department of <a href="/wiki/Computer_Science" class="mw-redirect" title="Computer Science">Computer Science</a>. Note the <a href="/wiki/Denazification" title="Denazification">effaced swastika</a> under the eagle</div></div></div>
<p>On the night of 11/12 September 1944, eighty per cent of the city, including many of the university's buildings, were destroyed during a bomb attack. For a short period in 1945, parts of the TH Darmstadt may have been closed by decree of the <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allies</a> before it was reopened in 1946. The electrical engineering department remained continuously functional, doing work under contract with the U.S. Army to build components of the V-2 guidance system. "But we have to be careful how we word this production order because we don't want the Russians to know that we are cranking up the V-2 system."<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In spite of the difficult post-war situation, university staff and students alike managed to settle down to university work in the severely damaged buildings, which had to be used as a makeshift solution.<sup id="cite_ref-:18_24-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:18-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As early as 1947, <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i> hosted the first <i>Internationaler Kongress für Ingenieurausbildung</i> (International Congress on Engineering Education), at which the participants discussed the moral responsibility of the technical intelligentsia and of the scientific elite in politics and society. In view of the disastrous consequences of the war, the participants (with the exception of the Americans, who had already contracted with THD faculty to continue weapon development), committed themselves henceforth to do research and teaching in engineering and scientific disciplines solely for the peaceful development of mankind.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:18_24-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:18-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<pre> 1. Technical Science as Ethical and Cultural Task.
 2. Present State and Tendencies of Development in Engineering Education Throughout the World.
 3. Selection of Students and Social Problems.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>
</pre>
<p>The speech delivered by Dr. James R. Newman, Director of American Military Government of Hessen, however, made no mention of such a commitment, while stating that:
</p><p>"An interchange of these [past experience], together with ideas and methods of education along engineering lines, will aid greatly, not only in the reconstruction of battle torn countries, but also in the bringing about of a universal understanding and mutual respect, and the charity which have prevented the understanding, the tolerance, the respect, and the charity so necessary for the peace, happiness, and contentment that is the dream of every human being on this earth."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The post-war period of reconstruction was largely based on a major development programme in the 1960s, by means of which universities and the state reacted to the continuously rising numbers of students. Since almost no land was available in the city centre for new construction projects, the decision was taken in 1963 to use the 'Lichtwiese' (a former airfield on the outskirts of the city) as a site for building extensions to the <i>Technische Hochschule</i>. Thus in the late 1960s and in the early 1970s numerous buildings, including a new student cafeteria, were erected there and ultimately became the university's second campus.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_reforms_in_the_1970s">University reforms in the 1970s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: University reforms in the 1970s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>After 1968 the university reform, having been initiated by the student movement, was beginning to take shape both at a national and a regional level. It aimed at creating clear university structures and the involvement of all university members in decision-making processes. In 1970 the <i>Hessisches Hochschulgesetz</i> (Higher Education Law of the Federal State of <a href="/wiki/Hessen" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessen">Hessen</a>) came into force. These gave <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i>, along with other Hessian universities, a new structure based on the introduction of a presidential statute and a unified administration as well as the subdivision of the university structure into departments.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:19_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:19-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In the mid 1970s, there was another rapid rise in student numbers. Staff development, however, lagged far behind, resulting in inevitable restrictions on admission imposed either by the central government or by the University. Regardless of the staff's heavy workload, the TH Darmstadt managed to set the course for the future, as evidenced by the School of Information Science, established in 1974, the <i>Zentrum für Interdisziplinäre Technikforschung</i> (Centre for Interdisciplinary Studies on Technology), founded in 1987, and the Department of Materials Science, established in 1989. This department has been housed in a new building on the Lichtwiese since 1996.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:19_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:19-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Renaming">Renaming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Renaming">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By the end of the 20th century, <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i> had been granted the legal status of a university, and had been offering a correspondingly wide range of subjects, for over a hundred years. For these reasons, and also with the objective of sharpening public awareness of the university's status at home and abroad, <i>Technische Hochschule Darmstadt</i> was renamed <i>Technische Universität Darmstadt</i> (which is also its official English name albeit often called <i>Darmstadt University of Technology</i>) on 1 October 1997. This name change was partly prompted by misunderstandings that had occurred in English-speaking countries, where <i><a href="/wiki/Technische_Hochschule" title="Technische Hochschule">Technische Hochschule</a></i> had often been mistakenly transliterated as 'Technical High School', providing a totally misleading connotation.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:16_22-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:16-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Autonomy_and_TUD_Law">Autonomy and TUD Law</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Autonomy and TUD Law">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On 1 January 2005, the first version of the TUD Law applied making TU Darmstadt the first German public university to be given administrative autonomy.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> New administrative structures were put into place, and their success is being evaluated. For instance, the university can now autonomously administer its budget and buildings. Also, the university can hire professors and negotiate their salaries by itself. Formerly this was done by the <a href="/wiki/Hessen" class="mw-redirect" title="Hessen">State of Hessen</a>. The status of autonomy also allows TU Darmstadt to invest in business start-ups.<sup id="cite_ref-:11_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The Technische Universität Darmstadt is the only German university that has legally committed itself to guarantee their students good studying conditions.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:12_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The TUD law in its current state has legal force up to 31. December 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-:20_20-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:20-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:11_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:11-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:12_34-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:12-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_university_as_a_pioneer">The university as a pioneer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The university as a pioneer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1882, the Technische Hochschule Darmstadt was the first university in the world to set up a chair for <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a> and founded the first faculty for it in 1883.<sup id="cite_ref-:21_6-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:21-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:10_5-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> The first chair holder was Erasmus Kittler.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In the same year the university introduced the world's first course of study in electrical engineering.<sup id="cite_ref-:10_5-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:10-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1913, the university set up the first chair for <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a> technology in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> The TH Darmstadt set up the first chair for scientific policy in 1951.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The first chair holder was <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Kogon" title="Eugen Kogon">Eugen Kogon</a>. He is considered one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a> in Germany. The TH Darmstadt shaped the subject of corporate governance in Germany. In 1973, the university established the first chair for management control system in Germany. The first chair holder was Peter Horvarth.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In Germany, the beginnings of <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> go back to the Institute for Practical Mathematics of the TH Darmstadt, which the mathematician Alwin Walther built in early 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 1956, the first programming lectures and internships in Germany were offered at the TH Darmstadt.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Due to the reputation that the TH Darmstadt had at the time in computer science research, the first international congress on computer science held in German-speaking countries took place in October 1955 at the TH Darmstadt.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Robert Piloty, professor at the TH Darmstadt, developed the computer science courses in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> In 1968, the TH Darmstadt introduced the first course of study in computer science in Germany and in 1975 the first business informatics course.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_40-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">Artificial intelligence</a> as a scientific field in Germany and Europe was founded by <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Bibel" title="Wolfgang Bibel">Wolfgang Bibel</a>, professor of intellectics at the TU Darmstadt.<sup id="cite_ref-:02_40-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:02-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> He set up a research group for artificial intelligence at the TH Darmstadt in 1988.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In 1996, the first chair in Germany for renewable energies was set up at TH Darmstadt and staffed with Thomas Hartkopf.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2004, it became the first German university to be declared as an autonomous university.<sup id="cite_ref-:22_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:22-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academic_profile">Academic profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Academic profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Departments">Departments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Departments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Typical for a <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">university of technology</a>, ten out of its 13 <a href="/wiki/Faculty_(division)" title="Faculty (division)">academic departments</a> (Fachbereiche) are in <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_science" title="Natural science">natural sciences</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mathematics" title="Mathematics">mathematics</a>, while three departments are in the <a href="/wiki/Social_sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="Social sciences">social sciences</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Humanities" title="Humanities">humanities</a>. The departments (with number of the department) are:<sup id="cite_ref-departments_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-departments-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Architecture (15)</li>
<li>Civil and Environmental Engineering (13)</li>
<li>Biology (10)</li>
<li>Chemistry (7)</li>
<li>Electrical Engineering and Information Technology (18)</li>
<li>History and Social Sciences (2)</li>
<li>Human Sciences (3)</li>
<li>Computer Science (20)</li>
<li>Mechanical Engineering (16)</li>
<li>Materials and Earth Sciences (11)</li>
<li>Mathematics (4)</li>
<li>Physics (5)</li>
<li>Law and Economics (1)</li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fields_of_study">Fields of study</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Fields of study">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>There are five fields of study (<i>Studienbereiche</i>), which offer <a href="/wiki/Interdisciplinarity" title="Interdisciplinarity">interdisciplinary</a> degree courses in which students take lectures in multiple departments:<sup id="cite_ref-departments_43-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-departments-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul><li>Computational Engineering</li>
<li>Energy Science and Engineering</li>
<li>Information Systems Engineering</li>
<li>Mechanics</li>
<li>Mechatronics</li></ul>
<p>TU Darmstadt offers about 100 courses of studies.<sup id="cite_ref-:3_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Beyond Bachelor's and Master's degrees, it also offers degree courses for teaching positions at German <a href="/wiki/Vocational_school" title="Vocational school">vocational schools</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gymnasium_(Germany)" title="Gymnasium (Germany)">gymnasiums</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_profile">Research profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Research profile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TU Darmstadt defined six profile areas which characterize its research profile:<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> 
</p>
<ul><li>Thermo-Fluids and Interfaces<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Future Energy Systems<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>From Material to Product Innovation<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Cybersecurity (CYSEC)<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Internet and Digitisation<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Matter and Radiation Science<sup id="cite_ref-fcnrs_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fcnrs-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>At the TU Darmstadt there are several <i><a href="/wiki/Sonderforschungsbereiche" class="mw-redirect" title="Sonderforschungsbereiche">Sonderforschungsbereiche</a></i> (SFB, collaborative research units)<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> as well as several <i><a href="/wiki/Graduiertenkolleg" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduiertenkolleg">Graduiertenkollegs</a></i> (graduate schools),<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> funded by <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Forschungsgemeinschaft" title="Deutsche Forschungsgemeinschaft">Deutsche Forschungsgemeinschaft</a>.
</p><p>The university has attracted a considerable number of national and international research institutions to the <i>Wissenschaftsstadt Darmstadt</i> (Darmstadt - City of Science). Among them are: 
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/GSI_Helmholtz_Centre_for_Heavy_Ion_Research" title="GSI Helmholtz Centre for Heavy Ion Research">GSI Helmholtz Centre for Heavy Ion Research (GSI)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Fraunhofer_Society" title="Fraunhofer Society">Fraunhofer Institute</a> for Secure Information Technology SIT<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Fraunhofer Institute for Computer Graphics Research IGD<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Fraunhofer Institute for Structural Durablity and System Reliability<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Space_Operations_Centre" title="European Space Operations Centre">European Space Operations Centre (ESOC)</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/European_Organisation_for_the_Exploitation_of_Meteorological_Satellites" title="European Organisation for the Exploitation of Meteorological Satellites">European Organisation for the Exploitation of Meteorological Satellite (EUMETSAT)</a>.</li>
<li>National Research Center for Applied Cybersecurity (CRISP)</li></ul>
<p>TU Darmstadt collaborates with these research institutes on a broad basis. For instance, TU Darmstadt and GSI agreed on a strategic partnership, which includes collaboration in the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/Facility_for_Antiproton_and_Ion_Research" title="Facility for Antiproton and Ion Research">FAIR Facility for Antiproton and Ion Research</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The National Research Center for Applied Cybersecurity is a collaboration between TU Darmstadt, Fraunhofer Institute for Secure Information Technology, Fraunhofer Institute for Computer Graphics Research and the <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Darmstadt University of Applied Sciences">University of Applied Sciences Darmstadt</a>. This partnership represents the largest alliance of research institutes in the area of cybersecurity within Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-:9_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:9-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> has set up a research laboratory at TU Darmstadt, ESA_LAB@TU Darmstadt. It is the first research laboratory the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a> has set up at a German university.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>As of 2018 the TU Darmstadt has won the competition of the <a href="/wiki/European_Institute_of_Innovation_and_Technology" title="European Institute of Innovation and Technology">European Institute of Innovation and Technology (EIT)</a> and is building an Institute for <a href="/wiki/Manufacturing" title="Manufacturing">Manufacturing</a> together with 50 partners including <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>, <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a>, <a href="/wiki/KUKA" title="KUKA">KUKA</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Research_Centre_for_Artificial_Intelligence" title="German Research Centre for Artificial Intelligence">German Research Center for Artificial Intelligence</a> and <a href="/wiki/Volvo" title="Volvo">Volvo</a>. At Darmstadt there will be an EIT Manufacturing Innovation Hub.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Together with <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University Frankfurt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Johannes_Gutenberg_University_Mainz" title="Johannes Gutenberg University Mainz">Johannes Gutenberg University Mainz</a>, TU Darmstadt has formed the strategic Rhine-Main Universities alliance.<sup id="cite_ref-:2_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TU Darmstadt is involved in the <a href="/wiki/German_Universities_Excellence_Initiative" title="German Universities Excellence Initiative">German Excellence Initiative</a>. This initiative sponsored the Cluster of Excellence Smart Interfaces (2007-2014), the Graduate School of Computational Engineering and the Graduate School of Excellence Energy Science and Engineering. TU Darmstadt is also partially involved with the Cluster of Excellence Normative Orders, based at <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University Frankfurt</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-exzellenceAtTU_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-exzellenceAtTU-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cooperation_with_companies">Cooperation with companies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cooperation with companies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Technische Universität Darmstadt maintains several research collaborations with companies and research institutions. These include, for example:
</p>
<ul><li>PRORETA, a research collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental AG</a> whose goal is to develop driver assistance systems that avoid traffic accidents.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Intel" title="Intel">Intel</a> Collaborative Research Institute for Secure Computing (ICRI-SC), a joint institute of the Technische Universität Darmstadt and Intel, which deals with the security of <a href="/wiki/System_on_a_chip" title="System on a chip">system-on-a-chip (SoC)</a> platforms.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> It is the first Intel collaborative research center for IT security outside the USA.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>Intel Collaborative Research Institute for Collaborative Autonomous &amp; Resilient Systems (ICRI-CARS), a joint institute of the Technische Universität Darmstadt and Intel to study the security, privacy and safety of auto­no­mous systems that collaborate with each other.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/SAP_SE" title="SAP SE">SAP</a> Research, a cooperation with the software manufacturer SAP, which conducts research in various fields.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategic_partnerships">Strategic partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Strategic partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Technical University distinguishes between strategic alliances, a cooperative lab and a TU Darmstadt cooperation institute in strategic partnerships.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The TU Darmstadt maintains <b>strategic alliances</b> with the companies <a href="/wiki/Merck_Group" title="Merck Group">Merck</a>, <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Bahn" title="Deutsche Bahn">Deutsche Bahn</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_AG" title="Continental AG">Continental</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Robert Bosch GmbH</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siemens" title="Siemens">Siemens</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><b>Cooperative Labs</b> are research laboratories that are operated together with the partner and, as a rule, on the grounds of the TU Darmstadt. The labs conduct joint and interdisciplinary research into a defined but broad subject area.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Together with <a href="/wiki/Merck_Group" title="Merck Group">Merck</a>, the TU Darmstadt operates the Merck Lab, which has been investigating novel inorganic composite materials since 2006 that are suitable as printable components for electronic applications.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Selected strategic partnerships can also receive the status of a <b>TU Darmstadt cooperation institute</b> from the university management.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> Since 2012, the first TU Darmstadt cooperation institute has been the <a href="/wiki/DB_Schenker" title="DB Schenker">DB Schenker</a> Lab, whose goal is to expand joint research in the fields of transport and logistics and to additionally create relevant offers in the fields of teaching, training and university marketing.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_70-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Knowledge_transfer">Knowledge transfer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Knowledge transfer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TU Darmstadt pursues multiple paths for knowledge and technology transfer. The university's start-up center HIGHEST (Home of Innovation, GrowtH, EntrepreneurShip and Technology Management) provides support for founders from the university, with a focus on digital and high-tech start-ups.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> For cooperation with small and medium sized companies, TU Darmstadt set up a structured collaboration with Hessenmetall, the regional association of the machinery, electronic and automotive industry.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> Research funds from industry were 37 million Euros in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="High-performance_computer">High-performance computer</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: High-performance computer">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Technische Universität Darmstadt is one of the few German universities that have a <a href="/wiki/Supercomputer" title="Supercomputer">high-performance computer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> The high-performance computer Lichtenberg is named after <a href="/wiki/Georg_Christoph_Lichtenberg" title="Georg Christoph Lichtenberg">Georg Christoph Lichtenberg</a> and has a computing power of about 1 PetaFLOPS.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> For comparison, the currently fastest high-performance computer <a href="/wiki/Summit_(supercomputer)" title="Summit (supercomputer)">Summit</a> owns 148.6 PetaFLOPS (as of June 2019). In 2015 Lichtenberg was listed in the <a href="/wiki/TOP500" title="TOP500">TOP500</a> at rank 410.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> In 2017, the TU Darmstadt received 15 million euros from the federal government and state for the expansion of the Lichtenberg high-performance computer, the Lichtenberg II.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:13_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:13-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> This should have more than twice the power.<sup id="cite_ref-:132_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:132-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:14_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:14-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> Lichtenberg II will be used especially in the field of <a href="/wiki/Computational_engineering" title="Computational engineering">computational engineering</a>, which is a profile topic of the TU Darmstadt.
</p><p>The TU Darmstadt is also a member of the Competence Center for High Performance Computing in Hessen (HKHLR), an association of the <a href="/wiki/Goethe_University_Frankfurt" title="Goethe University Frankfurt">Goethe University Frankfurt am Main</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Giessen" title="University of Giessen">Justus Liebig University Giessen</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Marburg" title="University of Marburg">Philipps University Marburg</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Kassel" title="University of Kassel">University of Kassel</a> and the Technische Universität Darmstadt.<sup id="cite_ref-:15_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:15-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Each of the members has a high-performance computer.<sup id="cite_ref-:15_81-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:15-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> As a voting member TU Darmstadt represents Hessian interests in the Gauß-Allianz, the union of all supercomputers at the state level in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-:15_81-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:15-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campuses">Campuses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Campuses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The University, with 140 Buildings and an area of property of 600 acres (2.4&#160;km<sup>2</sup>),<sup id="cite_ref-facts_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facts-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> is concentrated at the two campuses, Inner City and Lichtwiese. But individual facilities can be found in other parts of Darmstadt and in <a href="/wiki/Griesheim_(Hesse)" class="mw-redirect" title="Griesheim (Hesse)">Griesheim</a>, a neighboring town.<sup id="cite_ref-map_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-map-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Inner_City_Campus">Inner City Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Inner City Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>This campus lies very central in Darmstadt and is easily reachable by <a href="/wiki/Trams_in_Darmstadt" title="Trams in Darmstadt">tram</a> and bus from every part of the city. The departments located here are Electrical Engineering and Information Technology (18), History and Social Sciences (2), Human Sciences (3), Computer Science (20), Mathematics (4), Physics (5) and Law and Economics (1).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_Lichtwiese">Campus Lichtwiese</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Campus Lichtwiese">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Lichtwiese lies in the eastern part of Darmstadt. It is reachable by bus and a nearby train station. The departments located here are Architecture (15), Civil Engineering and Geodesy (13), Chemistry (7), Mechanical Engineering (16) and Materials and Earth Sciences (11).<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Botanical_garden">Botanical garden</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Botanical garden">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Botanical_Garden_of_TU_Darmstadt" title="Botanical Garden of TU Darmstadt">Botanical Garden of TU Darmstadt</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Botanischer_Garten_der_TU_Darmstadt" class="mw-redirect" title="Botanischer Garten der TU Darmstadt">Botanical Garden of the TU Darmstadt</a> is located near the Lichtwiese Campus and the Department of Biology (10) is located here as well. With additional buildings of the Department of the Materials and Earth Sciences (11)<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and parts of the faculty of Chemical Engineering and Biotechnology of the <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Darmstadt University of Applied Sciences">Darmstadt University of Applied Sciences (h_da)</a><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> it makes for an additional smaller campus.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Griesheim">Griesheim</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Griesheim">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since 2005, TU Darmstadt owns the <a href="/wiki/Griesheim_Airport" title="Griesheim Airport">August Euler Airfield</a>, Germany's oldest airfield, for scientific purposes. It is named after its founder <a href="/wiki/August_Euler" title="August Euler">August Euler</a>, a <a href="/wiki/List_of_aviation_pioneers" title="List of aviation pioneers">pioneer aviator</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> The airfield is not only used to start planes, but also to conduct research on topics where wide spaces are needed, for example <a href="/wiki/Advanced_driver-assistance_systems" title="Advanced driver-assistance systems">driver assistance systems</a> and <a href="/wiki/Automotive_lighting" title="Automotive lighting">automotive lighting</a> are being tested here.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Located near the airfield are the <a href="/wiki/Wind_tunnel" title="Wind tunnel">wind tunnels</a> of TU Darmstadt.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 185px"><div style="width: 185px">
			<div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;"><div style="margin:25px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Griesheim_(ZCS_-_EDES)_AN2005697.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Griesheim_%28ZCS_-_EDES%29_AN2005697.jpg/150px-Griesheim_%28ZCS_-_EDES%29_AN2005697.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Griesheim_%28ZCS_-_EDES%29_AN2005697.jpg/225px-Griesheim_%28ZCS_-_EDES%29_AN2005697.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Griesheim_%28ZCS_-_EDES%29_AN2005697.jpg/300px-Griesheim_%28ZCS_-_EDES%29_AN2005697.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a></div></div>
			<div class="gallerytext">
<p>August Euler Airfield, 2011
</p>
			</div>
		</div></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Internationality">Internationality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Internationality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>With 18% (2017),<sup id="cite_ref-:3_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:3-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> the percentage of international students at the TU Darmstadt is clearly higher than the average of German universities of 13% (2017/18).<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> TU Darmstadt maintains partnership agreements with over 300 universities in 53 countries world-wide, which enable students to come to TU Darmstadt and to go abroad within their course of studies.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> For example, the Technische Universität Darmstadt has partnerships with the <a href="/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" title="Massachusetts Institute of Technology">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_California,_Berkeley" title="University of California, Berkeley">University of California, Berkeley</a>, <a href="/wiki/KU_Leuven" title="KU Leuven">Katholieke Universiteit Leuven</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nanyang_Technological_University" title="Nanyang Technological University">Nanyang Technological University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tsinghua_University" title="Tsinghua University">Tsinghua University</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seoul_National_University" title="Seoul National University">Seoul National University</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>With <a href="/wiki/Tongji_University" title="Tongji University">Tongji University Shanghai</a>, <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Tech" title="Virginia Tech">Virginia Polytechnic Institute and State University, Blacksburg, Virginia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Graz_University_of_Technology" title="Graz University of Technology">Graz University of Technology</a>, TU Darmstadt has developed strategic partnerships.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> 
</p><p>The university offers international (English-language) Master's programs<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> and a broad range of <a href="/wiki/Double_degree" title="Double degree">double degree</a> programs.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Mundus#Erasmus_Mundus_Joint_Programmes" title="Erasmus Mundus">Joint Master Programme</a> "International Cooperation in Urban Development (Mundus Urbano)" is offered together with <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Pierre_Mend%C3%A8s-France" class="mw-redirect" title="Université Pierre Mendès-France">Université Pierre Mendès-France</a>, <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Universidad_Internacional_de_Catalu%C3%B1a" class="extiw" title="es:Universidad Internacional de Cataluña">International University of Catalonia</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Universita_degli_Studi_di_Roma_Tor_Vergata" class="mw-redirect" title="Universita degli Studi di Roma Tor Vergata">Universita degli Studi di Roma Tor Vergata</a> as part of the <a href="/wiki/Erasmus_Mundus" title="Erasmus Mundus">Erasmus Mundus</a> programme of the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>TU Darmstadt is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Conference_of_European_Schools_for_Advanced_Engineering_Education_and_Research" class="mw-redirect" title="Conference of European Schools for Advanced Engineering Education and Research">Conference of European Schools for Advanced Engineering Education and Research</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:2_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:2-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Technische Universität Darmstadt has been awarded the title "European University" by the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a>. Together with 6 other European technical universities, the TU Darmstadt has formed the alliance UNITE! (University Network for Innovation, Technology and Engineering). The aim of the project is to create a trans-European campus, to introduce trans-European curricula, to promote scientific cooperation between the members and to strengthen knowledge transfer between the countries. The alliance includes <a href="/wiki/Aalto_University" title="Aalto University">Aalto University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/KTH_Royal_Institute_of_Technology" title="KTH Royal Institute of Technology">Royal Institute of Technology</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Grenoble_Institute_of_Technology" title="Grenoble Institute of Technology">National Polytechnic Institute of Grenoble</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_Turin" title="Polytechnic University of Turin">Polytechnic University of Turin</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Polytechnic_University_of_Catalonia" title="Polytechnic University of Catalonia">Polytechnic University of Catalonia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Lisbon" title="University of Lisbon">University of Lisbon</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:5_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:5-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Activities">Activities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Activities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>TU Darmstadt offers various recreational sports courses and operates three sports halls, a sports stadium including various fields, a swimming pool, and a fitness studio. The TU Darmstadt won the university competition of the German Olympic Sports Confederation for the third time in succession and has since been awarded the title of the most athletic university in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> There are manifold accredited student groups, ranging from the <a href="/wiki/Formula_SAE" title="Formula SAE">Formula SAE</a> TU Darmstadt Racing Team (DART), TU Darmstadt Space Technology (TUDSaT)<b>,</b> <a href="/wiki/Akaflieg_Darmstadt" title="Akaflieg Darmstadt">Akaflieg Darmstadt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Chaos_Computer_Club" title="Chaos Computer Club">Chaos Computer Club</a> to a theater group, an orchestra, and the campus radio AudioMax.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The annual <a href="/wiki/Job_fair" title="Job fair">job fair</a> <i>konaktiva</i>, which connects approximately 10,000 students with potential employers, is organized by volunteer students.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Students.27_representation"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Students'_representation">Students' representation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Students&#039; representation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Students at TU Darmstadt are represented by the students' parliament (<i>Studierendenparlament</i>, StuPa), which is elected annually and in turn elects the <a href="/wiki/AStA" title="AStA">General Students' Committee</a> (<i>Allgemeiner Studierendenausschuss</i>, AStA). The AStA is the students' government and engages in university politics and provides social and economic counseling for students. Moreover, it runs the café <i>60,3qm</i> ("60.3 square meters"), a beer garden and a club in the Ducal Palace, a store for office supplies, and a bicycle garage. In addition to the regular university curriculum, students can attend various non-credit courses held by students and coordinated by the AStA.
</p><p>Complementing the General Students' Committee, which represents all students enrolled at TU Darmstadt, the students of each department (<i>Fachschaft</i>) are represented by an elected students' council (<i>Fachschaftsrat</i>). Students of the <i>Fachschaft</i> participate in a number of committees of their department, such as the department's council (<i>Fachbereichsrat</i>), which consists of professors, students, academic staff and administrative staff.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legends">Legends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Legends">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Since the 1970s, the fictitious student Fritz Filter passed numerous examinations at the Department of Architecture before graduating with a <i><a href="/wiki/Diplom" title="Diplom">Diplom</a></i> degree in 2004. His thesis featured the design of the department building. Fritz Filter turned in multiple further architecture theses since then.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Housing">Housing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Housing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>A survey determined that in summer semester 2009 students in Darmstadt paid an <a href="/wiki/Arithmetic_mean" title="Arithmetic mean">arithmetic mean</a> of 321 euros a month for rent, heat and utilities. With the German average being 281 euros at the time, this made Darmstadt the sixth most expensive city for students in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> This value only includes students not living at home, not married and pursuing their first degree (referred to as "normal student" in the survey).<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> In this semester, on national average, 23.4% lived with their parents, 12.4% lived in a <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_residence" class="mw-redirect" title="Hall of residence">hall of residence</a>, 1.6% were <a href="/wiki/Sub-tenant#Sublease" class="mw-redirect" title="Sub-tenant">lodgers</a>, 25.8% were sharing a flat with others, 17.2% were living alone and 19.9% were sharing a flat with their partner.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are 2,512 beds in 9 halls of residence offered by the state-run student affairs organization <a href="/wiki/Studentenwerk" title="Studentenwerk">Studierendenwerk</a> Darmstadt for students of TU Darmstadt and <a href="/wiki/Darmstadt_University_of_Applied_Sciences" title="Darmstadt University of Applied Sciences">Darmstadt University of Applied Sciences</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reputation_and_ranking">Reputation and ranking</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Reputation and ranking">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="infobox vcard" style="width: 18em">
<tbody><tr>
<th colspan="2" class="n" style="text-align: center; font-size: 125%"><span class="fn"><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings" title="College and university rankings">University rankings</a></span>

</th></tr>

</tbody></table>
<p>Within Germany and Europe, the TU Darmstadt (in the overall ranking) and its faculties (in individual grades) regularly occupy top positions in rankings.
</p>
<ul><li>According to the <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a> 2020 the TU Darmstadt is one of the universities with the highest scientific impact in Germany and leads among the <a href="/wiki/Institute_of_technology" title="Institute of technology">technical universities</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> It belongs to the top 25 universities in Europe with the highest scientific impact.<sup id="cite_ref-:4_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:4-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The TU Darmstadt is considered to be the scientifically most impactful university for <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-:32_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:32-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> The TU Darmstadt secures the 9th place among the best universities of <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> in Europe.<sup id="cite_ref-:33_115-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:33-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the fields of <a href="/wiki/Cryptography" title="Cryptography">cryptography</a>, <a href="/wiki/IT_security" class="mw-redirect" title="IT security">IT security</a> and <a href="/wiki/Software_engineering" title="Software engineering">software engineering</a> TU Darmstadt is the leading European university even before the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Cambridge" title="University of Cambridge">University of Cambridge</a> and <a href="/wiki/ETH_Zurich" title="ETH Zurich">ETH Zurich</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_114-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the fields of <a href="/wiki/Artificial_intelligence" title="Artificial intelligence">artificial intelligence</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Machine_learning" title="Machine learning">machine learning</a>, <a href="/wiki/Computer_vision" title="Computer vision">computer vision</a> and <a href="/wiki/Natural_language_processing" title="Natural language processing">natural language processing</a> it ranks second among the European universities.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_114-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the university ranking 2018 of the <a href="/wiki/Wirtschaftswoche" title="Wirtschaftswoche">Wirtschaftswoche</a> the TU Darmstadt is considered to be the best university for <a href="/wiki/Business_informatics" title="Business informatics">business informatics</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Industrial_engineering" title="Industrial engineering">industrial engineering</a> it secures the 3rd place. In <a href="/wiki/Mechanical_engineering" title="Mechanical engineering">mechanical engineering</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">electrical engineering</a> TU Darmstadt places itself on 4th place.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>By <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS Graduate Employability Rankings</a> 2019 TU Darmstadt is ranked 3rd in Germany, 22nd in Europe and at 78th place (overall) in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-:6_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:6-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The TU Darmstadt occupies the 2nd place in the networking of employers and students among German universities.<sup id="cite_ref-:62_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:62-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the Research Ranking of the Association for Information Systems TU Darmstadt occupies the 16th place in business informatics worldwide, 3rd place in Europe after <a href="/wiki/Copenhagen_Business_School" title="Copenhagen Business School">Copenhagen Business School</a> and <a href="/wiki/London_School_of_Economics" title="London School of Economics">London School of Economics and Political Science</a> and 1st place in Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>The TU Darmstadt has the second highest employment rate among its graduates compared to all graduates of German universities.<sup id="cite_ref-:63_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:63-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>In the Humboldt-Ranking of the <a href="/wiki/Alexander_von_Humboldt_Foundation" title="Alexander von Humboldt Foundation">Alexander von Humboldt Foundation</a> the TU Darmstadt takes first place in the engineering sciences.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>According to the Stepstone salary report for graduates 2017 TU Darmstadt graduates earn the highest salary in engineering and information technology in Germany in comparison with graduates of other German universities.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>According to the research report 2018 of the <a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Forschungsgemeinschaft" title="Deutsche Forschungsgemeinschaft">German Research Foundation</a> TU Darmstadt received Germany's highest third-party funding in the field of <a href="/wiki/Computer_science" title="Computer science">computer science</a> and in <a href="/wiki/Engineering" title="Engineering">engineering</a> the fourth highest third-party funding.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li>For several years, the Technische Universität Darmstadt has been one of the universities with the most top managers in the German economy. The university is currently among the top 3.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_faculty_and_alumni">Notable faculty and alumni</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Notable faculty and alumni">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:188px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg/186px-Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg" decoding="async" width="186" height="269" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg/279px-Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg/371px-Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2003" data-file-height="2900" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Peter_Gruenberg_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Peter_Gr%C3%BCnberg" title="Peter Grünberg">Peter Grünberg</a></div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Nobel_laureates">Nobel laureates</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Technische_Universit%C3%A4t_Darmstadt&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Nobel laureates">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates" title="List of Nobel laureates">Nobel laureates</a>, who studied, taught and researched at the TH/TU Darmstadt:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Gr%C3%BCnberg" title="Peter Grünberg">Peter Grünberg</a>, physicist and Nobel laureate in Physics (2007)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Horst_Ludwig_St%C3%B6rmer" title="Horst Ludwig Störmer">Horst Ludwig Störmer</a>, physicist and Nobel laureate in Physics (1988)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Herzberg" title="Gerhard Herzberg">Gerhard Herzberg</a>, chemist, physicist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1971)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Hermann_Staudinger" title="Hermann Staudinger">Hermann Staudinger</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1953)</li></ul>
<p>Taught at TH/TU Darmstadt through <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Merck_Lectureship" title="Emanuel Merck Lectureship">Emanuel Merck Lectureship</a>:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frances_Arnold" title="Frances Arnold">Frances H. Arnold</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (2018)<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:8_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Harry_Kroto" title="Harry Kroto">Harold Kroto</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1996)<sup id="cite_ref-:8_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jean-Marie_Lehn" title="Jean-Marie Lehn">Jean-Marie Lehn</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1987)<sup id="cite_ref-:8_128-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Manfred_Eigen" title="Manfred Eigen">Manfred Eigen</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1967)<sup id="cite_ref-:8_128-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:8-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<p>Other Nobel laureates are associated with the university:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gerhard_Ertl" title="Gerhard Ertl">Gerhard Ertl</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (2007)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/K._Alex_M%C3%BCller" title="K. Alex Müller">K. Alex Müller</a>, physicist and Nobel laureate in Physics (1987)<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Karl_Ziegler" title="Karl Ziegler">Karl Ziegler</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1963)<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Otto_Hahn" title="Otto Hahn">Otto Hahn</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1944)<sup id="cite_ref-:7_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Carl_Bosch" title="Carl Bosch">Carl Bosch</a>, chemist, engineer and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1931)<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Richard_Willst%C3%A4tter" title="Richard Willstätter">Richard Willstätter</a>, chemist and Nobel laureate in Chemistry (1915)<sup id="cite_ref-:7_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:7-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:188px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg/186px-MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg" decoding="async" width="186" height="279" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg/279px-MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5f/MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg/372px-MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1772" data-file-height="2658" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MEDIA_1907_Oliver_Zipse.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chairman of the Board of Management of <a href="/wiki/BMW" title="BMW">BMW AG</a></div></div></div>
